  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_cf3270c7-1f8d-49cf-a349-f996479fffbc'
      });
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer11704684405788685117"><b>Complete 5 Golden Stars</b><br/><br/><br/>"the Penultimate Pendragon"<br/>(as MacHale said, I like the ring to it, don't you?)<br/>was Epic!<br/><br/><br/><i>"The war wasn’t over. The story didn’t end there. Not for Bobby. Not for Saint Dane.<br/>And not for us."</i><br/>(from Preface of the book, MacHale)<br/><br/><br/>the battle of the Second Earth, home territory of the lead Traveler,<br/><br/>& Pendragon is nowhere to be found...<br/><br/>oh! another thing! Bobby is 18 now.<br/><br/>this book was a constant blending of actions, thrills, riddles & unraveling them, feelz attack & tensions, & thing</span>
  <span id="freeText11704684405788685117" style="display:none"><b>Complete 5 Golden Stars</b><br /><br /><br />"the Penultimate Pendragon"<br />(as MacHale said, I like the ring to it, don't you?)<br />was Epic!<br /><br /><br /><i>"The war wasn’t over. The story didn’t end there. Not for Bobby. Not for Saint Dane.<br />And not for us."</i><br />(from Preface of the book, MacHale)<br /><br /><br />the battle of the Second Earth, home territory of the lead Traveler,<br /><br />&amp; Pendragon is nowhere to be found...<br /><br />oh! another thing! Bobby is 18 now.<br /><br />this book was a constant blending of actions, thrills, riddles &amp; unraveling them, feelz attack &amp; tensions, &amp; things happening so fast, everyone was in a rush, I couldn't believe how much can happen in 500+ book, I also couldn't put the book down, even in my 3rd read, &amp; it was just as exciting/shocking as the first time.<br /><br />&amp; something just been revealed in re-reading, if you are watchful enough, seeing through the layers of the Plot the author carefully created &amp; can remember previous books while reading this one (it's the skill earned just by re-reading) you can see the clues that were there since the beginning. it's a complicated job! delicate work to see those threads &amp; delicate work for author to planting them in the first place.<br /><br />I cried a lot...<br />hair-raising &amp; extreme<br />tears &amp; laughs<br />serious &amp; dark<br />familiar faces &amp; reunions<br />unexpected turns of events &amp; that damn moment that ruined everything (I didn't blame him, I would done the same, probably?)<br /><br />one of the greatest changes happened in this book is the narration, something like end of book 5, but in larger scales!<br />New POV characters who we know already (yesss! Patrick &amp; Alder have their own POV!)<br />there's a lot going on concurrently, the decision Bobby made in the last book, revealing its consequences<br />the chaos, as we are near the end, parallel stories<br /><br />the end was emotional, unexpected, shocking, thrilling &amp; beautiful<br />that one last part &amp; I was crying the whole time, I was waiting for it for so long.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11704684405788685117" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13702506369476546541">Raven Rise (Pendragon, #9), D.J. MacHale<br/>Raven Rise is the ninth book in The Pendragon Adventure by D.J. MacHale. It was published on May 20, 2008. The book begins with separate narratives focusing on Patrick Mac and Alder, the Travelers of Third Earth and Denduron respectively. It follows the changes in their home territories and their realization that they are without Bobby Pendragon. On Denduron, the Bedoowan and Milago tribe are using the explosive tak that Bobby unearthed with a dygo from Za</span>
  <span id="freeText13702506369476546541" style="display:none">Raven Rise (Pendragon, #9), D.J. MacHale<br />Raven Rise is the ninth book in The Pendragon Adventure by D.J. MacHale. It was published on May 20, 2008. The book begins with separate narratives focusing on Patrick Mac and Alder, the Travelers of Third Earth and Denduron respectively. It follows the changes in their home territories and their realization that they are without Bobby Pendragon. On Denduron, the Bedoowan and Milago tribe are using the explosive tak that Bobby unearthed with a dygo from Zadaa to start a war with a neighboring tribe, the Lowsee tribe. On Third Earth, the once Utopian planet has morphed into a waste world. Bobby Pendragon, meanwhile, has been living comfortably on Ibara, the island community located on Veelox. Pendragon's own description states that he has been a contributor and leader of the rebuilding of Ibara, which was destroyed in the previous book by Saint Dane's Dimond Alpha Digital Organization D.A.D.O.army. Days after an unsettling conversation with Saint Dane, Pendragon encounters a drifting skimmer bearing a dying passenger on board (this passenger being Loque, one of the Jakills from The Pilgrims of Rayne who amazingly survived having a large amount of broken glass fall on him and slaving underneath Saint Dane while trying to dig up the flume in Rubic City along with the other Flighters). After hearing Loque's story, Bobby assumes that Saint Dane is after the flume and decides to prevent the flume from being reopened. He fails, and later discovers that Nevva Winter, Saint Dane's ally, has been living on Ibara disguised as Tribune Genj's daughter, Telleo, whom she killed months before. Hearing from her that Denduron is in danger, Bobby reluctantly sets out to rescue it. ...<br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز دوازدهم ماه نوامبر سال 2014 میلادی<br />عنوان: پندراگن: کتاب نهم: آرمانشهر کلاغ؛ نویسنده: دی.جی. مک هیل؛ مترجم: حسین شهرابی؛ مشخصات نشر: تهران، تندیس، 1393، در 592 ص، شابک: 9786001821288؛ موضوع: داستانهای ماجراجویانه از نویسندگان امریکایی سده 21 م<br />در «آرمان‌شهر کلاغ»، همه ی «هالا»، به خطر افتاده؛ اما بابی پندراگن در این میان غایب است: بابی در «ایبارا» گیر افتاده، و خیال می‌کند «سنت دین» را هم، همراه با خود در آن‌جا زندانی کرده است. اما نبرد، به قلمروِ زادگاهش: زمین دوم، رسیده است. «مارک دایمند» و «کورتنی چتویند»، برای شکست دادن نیروهای «سنت‌‌ دین» در زمین، دست تنها مانده اند. آن‌ها باید با رهبرِ فرقه ای توانمند، رودررو شوند، که با افشای رازی بزرگ، به مردمِان زمین، خود را محبوب و مشهور کرده است. زمینی‌ها تنها نیستند، و قلمروهای دیگری هم هستند. همگرایی، دیوارِ میانِ قلمروها را از میان برمی‌دارد، و چیزی نمانده که آخرین مرحله‌ ی نبردِ «سنت دین»، برای حکم‌رانی بر «هالا»، به پایان برسد. اما بابی هنوز پیدایش نیست. ... ا. شربیانی</span>

<div id="review_2261217207" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2261217207" />
    <a title="Lauren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4617391-lauren"><img alt="Lauren" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495435758p2/4617391.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2261217207?book_show_action=true">Jan 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lauren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lauren" href="/user/show/4617391-lauren">Lauren</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4617391-lauren?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4617391-lauren?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4617391-lauren?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4617391-lauren?shelf=i-cried">i-cried</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4617391-lauren?shelf=2018">2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2261217207" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17635891390700039210">Well. When I started this particular Pendragon installment, I definitely wasn’t expecting to have an entire ending chapter that rivaled the amount I cried during Clockwork Princess’s epilogue, but here we are. (it wasn’t quite as much as CP2 but that’s just because that epilogue was the best ending ever) <br/><br/>Wow, this was such a crazy ride from beginning to end. My boyfriend only told me one thing when it came to this book and that was that it didn’t really take place in one single territory and now</span>
  <span id="freeText17635891390700039210" style="display:none">Well. When I started this particular Pendragon installment, I definitely wasn’t expecting to have an entire ending chapter that rivaled the amount I cried during Clockwork Princess’s epilogue, but here we are. (it wasn’t quite as much as CP2 but that’s just because that epilogue was the best ending ever) <br /><br />Wow, this was such a crazy ride from beginning to end. My boyfriend only told me one thing when it came to this book and that was that it didn’t really take place in one single territory and now I completely understand why he told me that. It wasn’t like the others where we were introduced to a new world and a new challenge, this one progressed the story line so much and really finalized a lot.<br /><br />The second half of the book just kind of left me shocked and the book as a whole gave me an eerie feeling of witnessing the world during Hitler’s rise to power. The tattoos, the flags, the sense of “superior” human beings. It honestly kinda left me shuddering on more than one occasion while reading certain parts. <br /><br />Bobby finally gets reunited with his best friends- Mark and Courtney- only to be ripped away again almost as quickly. He and Alder make a daring journey in an attempt to stop so much bad from happening, only to be screwed at every turn. There were a couple times where I honestly found myself getting lured into believing one way, starting to get comfortable, when something would come up out of nowhere and leave me feeling like a complete idiot for being lured into that false sense of security.<br /><br />I could feel Bobby’s frustration, his anger, his sadness, all of it throughout this book. His emotions kept rising and rising and I could feel his blind hatred when it came to him being on that helicopter in that last bit. His whole existence is a question, he’s terrified of what’s at stake beyond just him being real or not, he’s angry at all the friend’s he’s lost and his unfair disadvantage when it comes to this whole war. This is where you really start to see Bobby being screwed over yet again when he comes back to the fight and it’s so hard to see him lose as much as he has with very little complaining. He’s such an amazingly strong and strong-willed person, it hurts to see the way he’s hurt time and time again.<br /><br />That last bit, the last chapter, I cannot even begin to explain how utterly huge and devastating that chapter was for me. You don’t realize how much you start loving these characters, rooting for them and their mission, hoping that you don’t have to watch them die. They’re all some of the most amazing characters and they’re all so unique compared to each other, he does such a good job making sure they’re all their own people and I love that. <br /><br />This was an amazing penultimate book and I cannot wait to read the last one to see how everything ends up wrapping up in the end. I already have it sitting next to me and I could not be more excited.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17635891390700039210" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3436930544479794614">Wow.<br/><br/>What a weird ending.<br/><br/>This is by far one of my favorite Pendragon books, hands-down. The beginning was, well, not really that much of a surprise, but it still was, um, a little sad. I couldn't put this book down, seriously. <br/><br/>Spoilers:<br/><br/>When Alder died, I effin' sobbed my heart out. He's my favorite character (besides Spader and Siry~), so it was gut-wrenching.<br/><br/>And the giant flume?! Holy cupcakes, that was weird! Awesome to a "T" but pretty scary. How could Naymeer, Saint Dane, and Nevva do that?! </span>
  <span id="freeText3436930544479794614" style="display:none">Wow.<br /><br />What a weird ending.<br /><br />This is by far one of my favorite Pendragon books, hands-down. The beginning was, well, not really that much of a surprise, but it still was, um, a little sad. I couldn't put this book down, seriously. <br /><br />Spoilers:<br /><br />When Alder died, I effin' sobbed my heart out. He's my favorite character (besides Spader and Siry~), so it was gut-wrenching.<br /><br />And the giant flume?! Holy cupcakes, that was weird! Awesome to a "T" but pretty scary. How could Naymeer, Saint Dane, and Nevva do that?! The Ravinians are scary people. :/<br /><br />The ending, though, had to be one of the strangest things I've ever read. Where in Halla were they?! When Spader came back I was like *foam*. It was crazy awesome, seeing everyone alive again! [Meaning Kasha and Press. :D]<br /><br />But seriously, this book was awesome. Can't wait for the next one!</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1600867033" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer10246966300805959706">My biggest flaw with these books is the promise of answers. The promise of all the answers will be revealed but as the books progressed, we had none. We were still in. The dark about everything and everyone, so let’s see if it can be made up for in the last book. Alder and Spader are my faves</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_178175353" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/178175353" />
    <a title="Aparajitabasu" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4790652-aparajitabasu"><img alt="Aparajitabasu" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1311701802p2/4790652.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/178175353?book_show_action=true">Jun 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aparajitabasu" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aparajitabasu" href="/user/show/4790652-aparajitabasu">Aparajitabasu</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4790652-aparajitabasu?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4790652-aparajitabasu?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4790652-aparajitabasu?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4790652-aparajitabasu?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4790652-aparajitabasu?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4790652-aparajitabasu?shelf=children-s">children-s</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer178175353" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9630381162363099044">The long Pendragon series is about to end. Its the penultimate book <i>
  <b>#9 Raven Rise</b>
</i> and its getting ugly and its also getting dystopic. Which is my kind of good. Lets read,<br/><br/>Here is the summary of the book:<br/><br/><i>This is where it begins. The showdown for Halla. At stake is nothing less than all that ever was and all that will be. There's only one thing missing--Bobby Pendragon. While Bobby remains trapped on Ibara, the battle moves to his home territory: Second Earth. Mark Dimond and Courtney Chetwynde</i></span>
  <span id="freeText9630381162363099044" style="display:none">The long Pendragon series is about to end. Its the penultimate book <i>
  <b>#9 Raven Rise</b>
</i> and its getting ugly and its also getting dystopic. Which is my kind of good. Lets read,<br /><br />Here is the summary of the book:<br /><br /><i>This is where it begins. The showdown for Halla. At stake is nothing less than all that ever was and all that will be. There's only one thing missing--Bobby Pendragon. While Bobby remains trapped on Ibara, the battle moves to his home territory: Second Earth. Mark Dimond and Courtney Chetwynde are left on their own to defend Second Earth agsinst the forces of Saint Dane. They must face off against a charismatic cult leader who has risen to power by revealing a shattering truth to the people of Earth: They are not alone. The Convergence has broken down the walls. The territories are on a collision course. The final phase of Saint Dane's quest to rule Halla is under way. And Bobby Pendragon is nowhere to be found.</i><br /><br />The story starts after Bobby trapped himself and demonic Saint Dane on the tropical Ibara, yet it seems that his sacrifice was pointless for the Convergence has already begun. On Third Earth, Patrick wakes up to a dystopian future Earth. He meets up with Mark and Courtney in 1930 and they go to Second Earth to try and stop Saint Dane's plans. Nevva is disguised as Telleo (trying to get Bobby to fall in love with her; no luck) and lets a few minor details slip. Bobby then finds out that Saint Dane has escaped Ibara, and goes after his to his home territory Second Earth. A cult leader named Alexander Naymeer (an English idealist, brainwashed by Saint Dane) is creating chaos with Ravinia (the name of the cult). Bobby, Alder, Mark, and Courtney try to avoid the Ravinians while looking for the leader of the rebellion. In a giant battle known as the Bronx Massacre almost half the characters die or at least seem to be dead (leaving clinchers for the next book), and Saint Dane seems to have won. Yet the ending gives readers hope for Bobby and the travelers.<br /><br />So literally all hell has broken loose. Although the previous book should be called for "where-all-hell-started-to-break-loose". D. J. Machale has completely discarded all the formula he used in the previous books and its chaotic and to some extent I've been expecting it since I began reading it, we'll take of this later. <br /><br />Bobby Pendragon is now grown and his decisions have not gotten any easier. The bond of friendships are still what make him such an endearing and flawed character. Halla is pretty chaotic and things are not as they are meant to be. That premise drives the book, shakes up former realities and brings us one step closer to understanding what is really going on in this Matrix-like world of adventure. (Just a ref. matrix is way better than this whole stuff)<br /><br />Although the first few (I said few since this series is not my favourite) books were amazing and real pageturners, this one was a bit hard to keep up with. machales writing style was not top quality and quite repetitive. it was like the entire series led up to this one book and everybody was expecting it to go out with a bang but it turned out to have a quite weak plot and did not live up to the reputation of the series. This installment of Pendragon is both exhilarating and disappointing all at the same time. There is so much going on and so much to take in from the past books that the bulk of adventure from any one territory is muted, which disappoints me because I love the individual experiences on each of the territories. I still am lingering on the past descriptive genius of unique territories such as Cloral and Eelong! The cool part is that the story line all still works well and I could not put this book down.<br /><br />I felt that this whole book was the lets watch the hero be stupid so that when he gets his act together later it will be more impressive part of the story. Now I can stand that for a chapter or two, but not a whole book. It got very old for me very quickly. All that you need form this book to get to the last one is a page or two on the few actions important to the plot. I do hope that the next book, the "hero has his act together". The battle is on in RAVEN RISE. The battle for Halla. The internal battle of Bobby Pendragon. The battle of the people of the territories. And the battle between Saint Dane and Pendragon. This is what it is all coming down to.<br /><br />Bottom line is its good but don't waste your money borrow it from a friend. (for those who found the book interesting please don't mind - this is an honest opinion that is all)</span>
  <a data-text-id="9630381162363099044" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_34824565" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/34824565" />
    <a title="Lacy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/977619-lacy"><img alt="Lacy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1227653219p2/977619.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/34824565?book_show_action=true">Oct 08, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lacy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lacy" href="/user/show/977619-lacy">Lacy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer34824565" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer103462620332267348">In the ninth installment of Bobby Pendragon's quest to save Halla from the clutches of Saint Dane, things go from crummy to worse. Mark and Courtney don't know what to believe when Saint Dane tells them that Bobby has given up the fight, don't know what they've started when Mark loses his traveler ring, and don't know what to do when they return to a Second Earth where nothing is as it once was.<br/><br/>These books are really interesting to me on a craft level. On the one hand, the plotting is top notch;</span>
  <span id="freeText103462620332267348" style="display:none">In the ninth installment of Bobby Pendragon's quest to save Halla from the clutches of Saint Dane, things go from crummy to worse. Mark and Courtney don't know what to believe when Saint Dane tells them that Bobby has given up the fight, don't know what they've started when Mark loses his traveler ring, and don't know what to do when they return to a Second Earth where nothing is as it once was.<br /><br />These books are really interesting to me on a craft level. On the one hand, the plotting is top notch; with most of this series, I think I see the final twist coming, I usually predict one right, and then WHAM! Something comes flying in out of left field that I never anticipated. But it doesn't feel like a cheat. It's just really excellent story telling.<br /><br />On the other hand, I find myself pretty much constantly annoyed with some of the actual writing. D.J. MacHale is a perfect example of telling instead of showing. What he normally does is show us something and then tell us about it. Several times. For example:<br /><br /><blockquote>"Welcome back," he said warmly, as if he actually meant it. "I was afraid you'd miss the festivities. Close your eyes; I'll put some lights on."<br /><br />What a courteous guy! He didn't want me to be uncomfortable when he flicked on the lights. How thoughtful. I'd have thanked him if I hadn't wanted to hurt him.</blockquote><br /><br />MacHale is trying for the easy conversationalism and sarcasm of Bobby's internal monologue, but really, he just succeeds in telling us the same thing twice. And he does it over and over and over again throughout the book. The tome's 544 pages could probably have been trimmed by a third by an editor with a canny eye. As it is, I spend a lot of time skimming with these books.<br /><br />Also, his tenses bother me. Everything Bobby writes in his journals is in the past tense. Everything. Even things that are still true. If he means, "I love Coke," as in, he still loves it even when he is writing the journal, he will nevertheless say "I loved Coke," as if the love had passed. I know, it's a grammarian thing, but it bugs the heck out of me and has for all nine books.<br /><br />But that's the interesting part. I still love the story. I'm still coming back for more. And I'm still REALLY disappointed that the last book of the series isn't out yet so I can run out and read it. <br /><br />Definitely good for guys, especially guys who like a series they can sink their teeth into. But girls will probably like it just as much. Hooray for female characters who kick ass!</span>
  <a data-text-id="103462620332267348" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17028970522021666952">WARNING!!! THIS REVIEW CONTAINS SPOILERS!!!!!!<br/><br/>This is probably my favorite one of the series!! I laughed, cried, and made people slightly scared for my sanity as I yelled "Oh that did NOT just happen!" This the second to last book in the series and holy mamba is it a doozy! As MacHale told me at the BEA Conference, the last 3 books are a series of their own because things really start to go down. I finally see what he means.   <span id="freeText17028970522021666952" style="display:none">WARNING!!! THIS REVIEW CONTAINS SPOILERS!!!!!!<br /><br />This is probably my favorite one of the series!! I laughed, cried, and made people slightly scared for my sanity as I yelled "Oh that did NOT just happen!" This the second to last book in the series and holy mamba is it a doozy! As MacHale told me at the BEA Conference, the last 3 books are a series of their own because things really start to go down. I finally see what he means. The fabric of Halla is disintegrating and at the start of the book, Bobby is out of play. <br /><br />You get to see the point of view of different travelers instead of just Mark, Courtney and Bobby. Things really start to get messed up on the territories as you try to figure out what exactly Saint Dane has planned. Things also get personal for Bobby, Mark and Courtney as the fight is taken to their home, Second Earth. <br /><br />The only thing I didn't quite understand was how Tello could be Nevva when Nevva took Mark's ring on First Earth and the entrance to the flume to Ibara was closed off. The only thing I could think of was that Saint Dane had the flume dug up long before we thought (or he did it faster than we thought since I don't think Tello went missing for a while). Overall, it wasn't really clear how this happened. <br /><br />Overall, this book gets 5/5 for me. Even with the confusion, this books was packed full of action, shock and awe! The ending, especially, will leave you in shock and awe. There is so much that happened but to keep from blathering on I will just say read the book and have the 10th handy, because you are just going to want to jump right into the next book :)</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5607809835745382813">Reviewed by Shyanne for TeensReadToo.com<br/><br/>RAVEN RISE is a wonderful addition to the PENDRAGON series. It is just as exciting as the rest and keeps you wanting more.   <span id="freeText5607809835745382813" style="display:none">Reviewed by Shyanne for TeensReadToo.com<br /><br />RAVEN RISE is a wonderful addition to the PENDRAGON series. It is just as exciting as the rest and keeps you wanting more. I had a hard time putting it down and there is no way that I will not be purchasing the next one so I can find out what happens next! <br /><br />RAVEN RISE is about a Traveler named Bobby Pendragon. Now eighteen, his struggle to save Halla is harder than ever, and everything he's ever done has come down to this. He must save Halla from an extremely evil man, Saint Dane, who is trying to merge all of the worlds into one. <br /><br />Saint Dane is not only trying to mix territories, which is something that Travelers are not supposed to do, but he is also trying to create the perfect group of people who will follow under him. What will he do with the "not perfect" people? He will take care of them. <br /><br />Saint Dane plans on controlling all of Halla, and he will decide what he thinks is right for the people of the territories. He believes he is doing right by deciding people's destinies for them and not letting them make their own decisions. Pendragon, on the other hand, thinks that people should make the decisions of their lives on their own. <br /><br />The battle is on in RAVEN RISE. The battle for Halla. The internal battle of Bobby Pendragon. The battle of the people of the territories. And the battle between Saint Dane and Pendragon. This is what it is all coming down to. <br /></span>

<div id="review_3295033475" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3295033475" />

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3295033475" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3915160456793698958">My reaction throughout reading the book and some of Bobby's decision making in this book. <br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1494311462ra/22702538.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>OH WOW !!! If this saga was a made into a TV show or Movie(s) like Harry Potter it would have a definite cult following, I swear because this series is mind blowing, so sad it was way ahead of its time!!! I desperately want to see a TV show made for this book!! EPIC EPIC EPIC !!!<br/><br/>Do you know why the movies/tv show (if it was ever made) would appeal to a lot of people ? <br/>Because unlike HP, this series comes wi</span>
  <span id="freeText3915160456793698958" style="display:none">My reaction throughout reading the book and some of Bobby's decision making in this book. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1494311462ra/22702538.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>OH WOW !!! If this saga was a made into a TV show or Movie(s) like Harry Potter it would have a definite cult following, I swear because this series is mind blowing, so sad it was way ahead of its time!!! I desperately want to see a TV show made for this book!! EPIC EPIC EPIC !!!<br><br>Do you know why the movies/tv show (if it was ever made) would appeal to a lot of people ? <br>Because unlike HP, this series comes with a lot of diversity in terms of race, age and species, it contains different time periods, it had different types of dimensions and every each Traveler has a story to tell, they matter. Even though Bobby is the main protagonist in this book, the other secondary characters are not just in the background, even if you are not a traveler you still play a important role. Unlike Harry Potter, almost all the main characters are played by one main race (or species), HP is the main story, that's the core story...its about HP, others besides Herminone and Ron, they all fall in the background (eventually). I'm not saying I don't like HP, it was a unique series of it own kind but I'm saying if this series/saga was given a chance, it would have a huge following like HP because it appeals to everyone. <br><br>----------*** Major Spoilers Alert***--------------<br><br>This is a LONG book !!! And it is also the most vital book because this time it is Earth that is trouble. Like I've mentioned before I was appalled by Bobby's final decision in previous book. I'm not going to lie but I will say this, I was disappointed he decided to do what he did. Although, seeing it from Bobby's POV, I understand why he did what he did. I mean come on, he was shoved into this adventure like being thrown into a pitch black room with a good luck wish. One party is given a torch and the other is ask to figure out without any aid. I understand Bobby felt like he did the best decision, he thought by trapping Saint Dane, he could stop the inevitable. Although even Bobby knew he was being rather selfish because he was tired of fighting. And the idea of Paradise life in Ibara was too appealing to leave behind. <br><br>This book was very long because a lot of the time, it had Bobby trying to convince himself that he did the right thing, even though in the back of his mind he felt it wasn't the best of decision. Ugh, I knew by mixing territories it was going to backfire in 10 folds. As soon as Alder return to Denduron, he knew trouble had already kick started in his territory and worse thing was, that he had no way of letting Bobby know what had happened. As soon as Bobby discovered Loque, reality start crushing in, Bobby started to realize the consequences of his decision making. One by one reality starts to fall in place and Bobby finally realize that he made the wrong call. However, it was a lil to late to do any saving for Ibara. Ugh, I do not want to be in Bobby's shoes at that time, to know that he got played right into Saint Dane's plan the whole time. Burn!!<br><br>I was so glad when Bobby decided to move forward and get back to Denduron, because if he had stayed and tried to work out a plan to save Ibara. It would have been useless battle. Bobby started to recall what Saint Dane told him long time ago, that Denduron will be the first to fall because the moment he saw how the people of Bedoowan and Milago are now doing the very thing they wanted to oppose in the first series. They become the aggressor to other tribes in Denduron and was loving it. Having no chance at stopping the turning point in Denduron, Bobby and Alder decided to leave that territory and try save others from falling especially Earth(s). <br><br>While this was happening to Bobby, Mark and Courtney was also having their own set of problems. Every decision they make is affecting both Bobby and other territories, especially Earth territories. While I don't blame Mark for what he did, a part of me wished that he had chosen the ring. Of course, nobody would willingly sacrifice their parents but part of me wished he had because again everything was playing right into SD's plan. You have to admit, Saint Dane and Nevva make an impressive villain. Ugh too good in fact they make you feel bad for wanting to oppose them. They make you feel stupid and useless, and boy they are VERY good at that.<br><br>With Patrick spilling his side of the story of what disastrous changes happened in Third Earth, he and the duo acolytes travel back to second earth. It's scary isn't it to leave behind your family in first earth and to know that you may NEVER see them again! The trio adventure in second earth is epic as it can be, imagine the world you left behind is no longer the same. Returning to a world that had altered so much because of your decision making in earth one. Ugh, I would have passed out from severe pressure! They later find out a dickbag call Naymeer who seem to know who Mark and Courtney and everything about flumes and territories and is spreading a new wave of cult of chosen people and encouraging the idea of marginalizing the not chosen! Typical isn't it, no matter what territories you are in or race or species the moment you are told you are special and given power, everything else is trash and worthless. We become indulged in the world of being "The ONE" the powerful and the Elite!! As much as I hate to say this, Saint Dane got a point though, if people are given the right opportunity they will destroy the very idea of basic morale values. Everyone is subject to their own greed and glory. However, that's where I end my agreement with him. Because Saint Dane creates this opportunity that wasn't there before, he pushes and shoves that "special" idea into people to start a chain of horrendous events that will bring their own downfall. <br><br>Saint Dane is like a fire to pot full of charcoal. The charcoal will remain as it is if there is no fire to ignite it. So what he does, he set fire to it and watch the charcoals catch fire and burn each others to dust. Then he turns around and say "Tadaa, I told you so" while strictly avoiding the fact that the charcoal will not burn turn to dust if there was never any fire in the first place ..............WOW pretty good analogy if I say so myself LOL!!<br><br>I don't want to go too much detail into everything that happened in this book, because IT IS SOOOOO LONG. However, I was glad when the duo acolytes and Bobby and along with Alder tried to fight the turning point in Second Earth. Although sadly it was very brief moment together because they again got separated again and the duo was banished into the unknown. The events that happened in Second Earth, felt more real because unlike other territories, you have a sense of fantasy vibe, and you only know one part of that territory, don't really find out much other things in that "planet". The Earth territory is basically our current reality, everything that happens is here and now. The involvement of our everyday technology, people and organization such as UN, makes it so real. Like this could happen to you too. <br><br>One thing that caught me off guard was the power the Traveler ring possessed. I mean, neither Bobby nor any other traveler even realize just how powerful that ring was. They only used it to guide themselves to find a flume and send mail but they never thought it could do so much more. Unfortunately for them, Neymaar had unlocked the key to the actual power of the ring. It kind of annoys me that even after witnessing the power demonstrated by Neymaar. Neither one of them ever thought of using the ring as a weapon. They could do the same had they were given some time to understand how it works. Although again, sadly time was not on their side.... wasn't it?. <br><br>HAHAHA, I knew it was her the whole time, why ? because everything was happening too smoothly, he was an ex member of Ravinia. And the obvious fact that he didn't even bother to ride together with them before heading to the stadium for the HUGE life changing event was also another red flag. I admit when Bobby lost his marbles on the helicopter, I knew he wasn't thinking straight anymore because if anything Saint Dane and Nevva works in a similar pattern. They use people, they disguise, they're very patient and they always put on an "act" that pushes Bobby to make all the wrong decision. Mostly, Saint Dane's lack of reaction should have been a dead give away to Bobby that killing Naymeer means nothing to him.....The old fart was only a pawn in his game. Hadn't Saint Dane repeatedly told Bobby that <b>he</b> will be the ultimate power? Do you think he gives a rats arse about Neymeer after the completion of the final turning point in Second Earth? If Bobby didn't kill Neymeer, pretty sure he would have killed that old fart himself. And Nevva, wow give this girl an Oscar award for her acting ability. She fooled him twice in this book !! OUCH<br><br>The EPIC scene of Bobby floating the the space watching all the flumes exploding.....was mind Blowing!!! I mean, to witness the very end of Halla happening right infront of his eyes. Dayum!!<br><br>Arghh finally Bobby meets Uncle Press!!! Woot!!! Uncle Press was right, Bobby <b>did</b> see him again as promised!!. And I love how every traveler appears one by one, everyone dead or alive is back again with Bobby. It was amazing !!! Uncle Press says that it is the right time to kill Saint Dane, since he believes that he has won. He also says that it is time for the current Travelers to learn the truth about themselves. Finally !!! OMG please tell me !!! Because I want to know everything about Travelers !!!!!!!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1441804853ra/16154940.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Loor finally kiss Bobby !!! Although it wasn't as intense as the "almost" kiss in Zadaa but still Bobby nearly fell over from the kiss !!! HAHAHAH Also Boy, I was glad you were loyal to your "strong" feelings for Loor because he didn't fall for Telleo's romantic advances even though he knew he might never see Loor again. SO SWEET !!!<br><br>Arghh........If there is one thing that slightly disappointed me in this book, it would be the fact that we never gotten Siry and Loor's POV after the events in IBARA. We had Alder's POV, when he got back to Denduron after he came back from Ibara. Although, I wish there was a brief moment where we had Siry's POV and realization that he can't go back to Ibara and is stuck in Zadaa. I wanted a lil bit information on what he did after that? Did he find Loor ? Because I don't think he knew other territories besides Denuron, Veelox and Zadaa. I wonder what happened in Zadaa after Loor found out what Bobby did. I guess Siry did find Loor because she was annoyed Bobby didn't come to her for help :P <br><br>I can't wait to read the final book and I'm so sad the series is ending already !!! I'm sad and excited at the same time!</span>

<div id="review_31602932" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/31602932" />
    <a title="Brigid ✩" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/886144-brigid"><img alt="Brigid ✩" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581869052p2/886144.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/31602932?book_show_action=true">Aug 30, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brigid ✩" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brigid ✩" href="/user/show/886144-brigid">Brigid ✩</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer31602932" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer452381834248085663">Okay ... I had to process this for, like, a day before I could come up with a review. My first reaction was like, O_o !!!!!! WTH??? But now that I've thought it over ... It wasn't so bad. It was definitely not my favorite of the series, but it wasn't horrendous. I just have a few issues with it.<br/><br/>First of all, it started off kinda slow. I mean, Pendragon didn't even show up for the first a hundred pages. What was with that? It was just a hundred pages of people running around going "WHERE'S PENDRA</span>
  <span id="freeText452381834248085663" style="display:none">Okay ... I had to process this for, like, a day before I could come up with a review. My first reaction was like, O_o !!!!!! WTH??? But now that I've thought it over ... It wasn't so bad. It was definitely not my favorite of the series, but it wasn't horrendous. I just have a few issues with it.<br /><br />First of all, it started off kinda slow. I mean, Pendragon didn't even show up for the first a hundred pages. What was with that? It was just a hundred pages of people running around going "WHERE'S PENDRAGON?? WHERE'S PENDRAGON???" And I'm like *yaawwwn* Soooo when is this going to pick up? I didn't feel like it ever DID pick up, either. Sure, there were a few weird plot twists here and there, but ... idk. There wasn't a lot to it.<br /><br />Secondly, adding onto that, it was much too long. It was like, six hundred pages long, and only had about two or three hundred pages worth of plot. Bigger isn't better, DJ MacHale!!! The structure of the plot and the writing seems to have gotten much more careless as the series has continued. There are the paragraphs that are like two words long, and then the run-on paragraphs that are like an entire page long! Plus there are far too many careless typos in these books, which adds to my doubt on the editor's part. I mean, the author wrote "read" when he was supposed to write "red"! Sorry, but that's, like, horrendous editing. It made me wince. Literally.<br /><br />Third, I have some issues with character development. I feel like Pendragon appealed to me more when he was a wimpy little kid. Now he's all like "Ooh I'm so awesome. I'm going to yell at people and strangle people." Does he seem a little arrogant now, or is it just me? He just sorta annoys me, at this point. Courtney and Mark annoy me, too, but for a different reason. While Pendragon has matured a little too much, I feel like Courtney and Mark are just MORE immature than when the series started out. They haven't really changed so much; they still act like fourteen-year-olds. I kept forgetting that they're, like, eighteen now. AGh. <br /><br />Okay, actually like all of the characters annoy me. Except for Loor. She's awesome. But she was only on, like, the last page. And it was the best page in the entire book. Ga haha. ;D Yeah, I kinda want Pendragon to end up with Loor. Cuz Courtney is really annoying, and he never sees her anyway!!<br /><br />All right, I'm getting carried away with this. Moving on.<br /><br />Lastly, WHAT THE HELL WAS WITH THE ENDING??? ****spoiler coming up*****<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />PENDRAGON DIED???? I'M SO CONFUSED!!! IT DIDN'T MAKE ANY FREAKING SENSE!!! I HAVE NO IDEA WHAT HAPPENED!!! GAAAH I'M GOING TO HAVE AN ANEURISM OVER THIS!!!!<br /><br />Oh well. I guess I'll have to read the last book. Anybody know when it comes out??</span>
  <a data-text-id="452381834248085663" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/71739516" />
    <a title="Victoria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2299764-victoria"><img alt="Victoria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1242771111p2/2299764.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/71739516?book_show_action=true">Sep 18, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Victoria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Victoria" href="/user/show/2299764-victoria">Victoria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer71739516" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2211044317811756278">This is the "penultimate Pendragon," as D.J. MacHale himself calls it. And boy, is it full of everything needed to lead into the final chapter of this series that literally spans all of space and time.<br/><br/>It has come back to Second Earth. Bobby, trapped on Ibara by his own hand, has a painful revelation to make. He hasn't stopped Saint Dane. Instead, the demon has freed himself and is now launching his final plan to bring about the Convergence and his ultimate goal. And he has, at last, chosen Bobby</span>
  <span id="freeText2211044317811756278" style="display:none">This is the "penultimate Pendragon," as D.J. MacHale himself calls it. And boy, is it full of everything needed to lead into the final chapter of this series that literally spans all of space and time.<br /><br />It has come back to Second Earth. Bobby, trapped on Ibara by his own hand, has a painful revelation to make. He hasn't stopped Saint Dane. Instead, the demon has freed himself and is now launching his final plan to bring about the Convergence and his ultimate goal. And he has, at last, chosen Bobby's home as the battleground.<br /><br />A terrifying cult leader named Alexander Naymeer brings millions under his sway, pointing Second Earth toward a vision of utopia with a horrifying dark side. Mark and Courtney struggle to keep their heads in the game even as their ties to Bobby pull them into the center of the conflict. Saint Dane and his accomplice Nevva Winter come up with the most brutal and fiendishly intelligent plans yet. And Bobby, fighting with the pain of his own duty, ethics, choices, and responsibilities, will either triumph or shatter beneath it all.<br /><br />Everything in this book is bigger. The series gets progressively darker, scarier, more suspenseful, more wrenching, more intense. Strange new twists get thrown in, things you weren't expecting at all. And the ending leaves you at the edge of a cliff at the end of all things, waiting to see what the final fight for Halla will bring. I am really counting on MacHale not to fumble this ending, and to take some of the strange concepts he's introduced and make them work well instead of fall flat. I can't wait!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2211044317811756278" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_526559847" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/526559847" />
    <a title="Madie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16863724-madie"><img alt="Madie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1463622173p2/16863724.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/526559847?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Madie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Madie" href="/user/show/16863724-madie">Madie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16863724-madie?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer526559847" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8786022093813188820">All right, so this Pendragon was quite the ride. With countless riveting twists and turns, it kept me on the edge of my seat for its entirety. Raven Rise is, I believe, one of my favorite installments in this series, because it pulls you in and doesn't let you go.<br/><br/>Some people say they were quite disappointed with Raven Rise; it was all over the place, too much was happening at once, and Bobby kept making the same arguments and excuses over and over. I just picked this book up after having started</span>
  <span id="freeText8786022093813188820" style="display:none">All right, so this Pendragon was quite the ride. With countless riveting twists and turns, it kept me on the edge of my seat for its entirety. Raven Rise is, I believe, one of my favorite installments in this series, because it pulls you in and doesn't let you go.<br /><br />Some people say they were quite disappointed with Raven Rise; it was all over the place, too much was happening at once, and Bobby kept making the same arguments and excuses over and over. I just picked this book up after having started the series several years ago, so I came into this installment not totally prepared for its intensity. Raven Rise is nothing like the other Pendragon books, and everything you may think you have learned throughout the series is uprooted and crushed to smithereens. It's sort of frustrating, and a little disconcerting, but it makes you feel exactly how Bobby feels, and I love that about this book.<br /><br />One of the highlights of reading this was, for me, acknowledging how different it is from the previous books in the series. Bobby has grown up, there's no way around it. He is no longer a naïve and somewhat volatile 14-year-old, he's eighteen, and he's got a lot on his plate. All of his friends do. That is what was so satisfying for me about this book; to see Bobby, Mark, Courtney and all the others starting to learn exactly what this whole crazy escapade is about. I'm definitely looking forward to running to the library (or the bookstore) and finding the tenth one - it's about time I finished this series!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8786022093813188820" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_19600909" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/19600909" />
    <a title="Ashley Brooke" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/456072-ashley-brooke"><img alt="Ashley Brooke" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1191614845p2/456072.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/19600909?book_show_action=true">Apr 06, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley Brooke" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley Brooke" href="/user/show/456072-ashley-brooke">Ashley Brooke</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Pendragon Fans (a given), Fans of action/fantasy in general</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer19600909" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8032229784187533146">The Pendragon series has been a favorite of mine ever since my mom sent me the ARC of Merchant of Death my freshman year of college. I remember picking it up to kill the morning and getting sucked in from page one. Needless to say, I stayed in most of the day reading it. Expectations were high for Raven Rise, for I think the two books before this were very well done. I'm happy to say that Raven Rise went beyond my expectations.<br/><br/>We all knew that Bobby's actions at the end of the last book were goi</span>
  <span id="freeText8032229784187533146" style="display:none">The Pendragon series has been a favorite of mine ever since my mom sent me the ARC of Merchant of Death my freshman year of college. I remember picking it up to kill the morning and getting sucked in from page one. Needless to say, I stayed in most of the day reading it. Expectations were high for Raven Rise, for I think the two books before this were very well done. I'm happy to say that Raven Rise went beyond my expectations.<br /><br />We all knew that Bobby's actions at the end of the last book were going to royally mess up Halla, but, never did I think they would impact the whole of Halla as much as it. In Raven Rise we travel along with multiple travelers to different territories, seeing the vast changes in Halla from many different point of views. <br /><br />The only problem that I had with the book, which might be a personal thing, was that there were some times where the constant narration grated on me. I wanted dialogue or some interaction between someone during some of the journal entries. That was only a minor problem, though.<br /><br />Raven Rise is action packed, as always, but also has moments where it really gets to you at an emotional level, or at least, it got to me. DJ has again written a book where you could laugh and cry and throughly enjoy the entire ride.<br /><br />4 stars from me. I hope you enjoy it as much as I did.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8032229784187533146" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/62159875?book_show_action=true">Jul 04, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jordan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jordan" href="/user/show/2308874-jordan">Jordan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer62159875" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10379590598856979941">OH IT WAS SO AWESOME!!! Ok, so maybe... well... I dunno. It didn't have the charm or the humour of the previous books. The concept was good, but it wasn't as good as it could've been... you know? It just felt like a continuation of the story, rather than pow pow pow OMGOSH I'M IN LOVE type of story. It was just... story. With some humour.<br/><br/>The pros: It was WAY more exciting. I was all like, "NO! BOBBY! DON'T DO IT! DON'T HURT THE BRITISH GUY!!" (read to understand) And then I cried at the end just</span>
  <span id="freeText10379590598856979941" style="display:none">OH IT WAS SO AWESOME!!! Ok, so maybe... well... I dunno. It didn't have the charm or the humour of the previous books. The concept was good, but it wasn't as good as it could've been... you know? It just felt like a continuation of the story, rather than pow pow pow OMGOSH I'M IN LOVE type of story. It was just... story. With some humour.<br /><br />The pros: It was WAY more exciting. I was all like, "NO! BOBBY! DON'T DO IT! DON'T HURT THE BRITISH GUY!!" (read to understand) And then I cried at the end just because of the utter... well, I'd say failure, but that might spoil things ;) It was so great and awesome and adventurous and shocking. Just not as amusing :(<br /><br />It's rating... Well, I think PG13. I don't remember WHAT was violent, really, but I remember thinking that it got a bit violent again. It had some... OH! I remember now. Ok, in one scene, there is a lot of blood/broken bones mentioned. It's not horrible exactly... but it's disturbing. Anyway. There does appear to be actual language. FOR THE FIRST TIME!! Sheesh! It wasn't awful at all, but I was shocked to see any at all. It didn't even feel natural. I think he just felt the need to add swear words. Nasty.<br /><br />So... not to spoil anything... but the end was good.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10379590598856979941" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText13702799103079173636" style="display:none">Yes, there is a tenth book, and no, Saint Dane is not dead. Yet. Hopefully. You get my point. In <i>Raven Rise,</i> the battle finally moves to Second Earth and Bobby partially has no idea because he lost his Traveler ring. Nevva Winter leads Bobby back to the other Flume on Ibara and gives him back his ring, however - not out of kindness, though, of course. Nonetheless, Bobby goes to Third Earth to find out everything he can about Saint Dane's 'Convergence' and ends up with the 'Bronx Massacre' after a lot of page-flipping....Unfortunately, Third Earth changed for the worst and is no longer high-tech. Anyhow, after receiving all the disturbing information he can handle, Bobby first goes to Denduron and rounds up Alder, and then goes back to Second Earth where he meets with the 'new' Traveler from Second Earth, (impossible, I know,) who is bent around Saint Dane's finger so much that it's disgusting. That's what you get when a demon saves your life...Well, Bobby and Alder do everything they can to save the people who haven't gone crazy on Second Earth, but to no avail. They find out soon enough how fast Halla can unravel... </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16218397699603895679">I am SO conflicted. On one hand I <i>love</i> it because the Saint Dane/Bobby stuff is really getting funny (they sound like old friends it's amazing) and Bobby's going insane, but on the other I'm just baffled at how stupidly easy it was for Nazis to take over the world.<br/><br/>NAZIS. True, honest-to-god <i>NAZIS</i>, master race, concentration camps and all. AND THEY TOOK OVER THE UNITED STATES OF AMERICA.<br/><br/><i>AND THE UNITED NATIONS.</i><br/><br/>HOW??????<br/><br/>I know this book is old. I <i>know</i> that. But the author never says the Second Eart</span>
  <span id="freeText16218397699603895679" style="display:none">I am SO conflicted. On one hand I <i>love</i> it because the Saint Dane/Bobby stuff is really getting funny (they sound like old friends it's amazing) and Bobby's going insane, but on the other I'm just baffled at how stupidly easy it was for Nazis to take over the world.<br /><br />NAZIS. True, honest-to-god <i>NAZIS</i>, master race, concentration camps and all. AND THEY TOOK OVER THE UNITED STATES OF AMERICA.<br /><br /><i>AND THE UNITED NATIONS.</i><br /><br />HOW??????<br /><br />I know this book is old. I <i>know</i> that. But the author never says the Second Earth year. That's a trick to make things timeless. So the logical thing is that he wanted me to imagine this is going on right now.<br /><br />And right now what's going on is that Western nations have become so thin-skinned that a white person wearing dreadlocks is considered racist, people imagine that unless you're a black lesbian there's no way you can write a black lesbian, and vice-versa, and the term 'nazi' is thrown at anyone remotely talking about minority crime rates and missing black fathers.<br /><br />NAZIS WOULD NEVER TAKE OVER. NEVEEEEEEER<br /><br />Even if we weren't in a SJW-infested era, do you honestly believe that Christians, conservatives, middle-class citizens, atheists, TEENAGERS, will just adhere to something that's more akin to Scientology, which is already a joke by itself, plus concentrations camps????<br /><br />NEVER HAPPEN<br /><br />THIS IS IDIOTIC<br /><br />WHY DIDN'T BOBBY TAKE BACK MARK'S RING???? IT WOULD'VE SOLVED EVERYTHING.<br /><br />AAAAHHHHH<br /><br />Like Hitler got were he was because Germany was already deep in the shithole after WWI and they had very little to lose. If Germany had been fine, WWII'd never have happened.<br /><br />But I still REALLY like this because it's the end of Bobby's rope. HE'S SO ANNOYED MY GOD GIVE HIM A SNACK ALREADY. And Saint Dane is just ???? FINALLY MORE TALKING. I want them to get stuck in a room together and argue all day. Give me just one frenemy episode and I will love you forever.<br /><br />So yes, still good except for the way Second Earth falls.<br /><br />WOULD NEVER HAPPEN EVER ARRRGGGHHHH<br /><br />Courtney was cool but whenever she cracked a joke I wanted to hit her. And couldn't Mark tell Nevva that if she went back and let his parents get on the plane, it would create a time paradox because if his parents aren't saved, he never goes to First Earth with Forge, the dados don't happen and the Convergence falls flat? Like bitch she got you so good. And I mean he leaves his parents anyway so I would've let it happen. I love my parents but the universe is more important you know?<br /><br />SHITS GETTING REAL AAAAHHHHH<br /><br />Gimme more Bobby/Saint Dane</span>

<div id="review_2024289993" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2024289993" />
    <a title="Nina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20966982-nina"><img alt="Nina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1496991380p2/20966982.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2024289993?book_show_action=true">Oct 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nina" href="/user/show/20966982-nina">Nina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781416914198" href="/book/show/6949315-raven-rise">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2024289993" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2228866403420690170">McHale knows exactly when the whole go-to-territories-find-the-turning-point-meet-Saint-Dane-and-then-save/fail-the-territory thing gets tedious. And after 9 books, I'd say it was getting there. To be fair, each book has set itself apart from its' predecessor by increasing the stakes. Some books were hit-and-miss for me, as I found some more tedious than interesting because it was formulaic, and either I had little interest in the territory Bobby was on (I'm looking at you, Eelong -- and world-b</span>
  <span id="freeText2228866403420690170" style="display:none">McHale knows exactly when the whole go-to-territories-find-the-turning-point-meet-Saint-Dane-and-then-save/fail-the-territory thing gets tedious. And after 9 books, I'd say it was getting there. To be fair, each book has set itself apart from its' predecessor by increasing the stakes. Some books were hit-and-miss for me, as I found some more tedious than interesting because it was formulaic, and either I had little interest in the territory Bobby was on (I'm looking at you, Eelong -- and world-building plays a BIG role in this series, mind).. or the book had way too much action, not enough plot (looking at you too, Quillan), and it just felt like mindless padding. I did really like <i> Pilgrims of Rayne though </i>.<br /><br />This book though. This book was faaaaaar from tedious, and I could barely put it down. Not only are the stakes increased, but the whole formula practically changes (not really, but it felt like it). All the previous books has led to this. Stakes were high form the get-go. Things were beyond bleak after the end of "Pilgrims of Rayne", and this book did not once let you, or the characters, take a breather. It just got bleaker and more desperate as it went on; pushing all the characters to their limits. Since it's set in practically our-Earth, there was little world building to be done, as it was already established. That meant McHale was able to pump this book with plot and motion. There was barely any action in this, which I loved, honestly. Things were <i>HAPPENING</i>. <br /><br />I loved how, the first third of the book, was everybody freaking out about how bad everything had gone thanks to Bobby after the previous book... all while Bobby was living out the dream retirement life in obliviousness. The focus on other characters aside from Bobby is something I've grown to love about the series. And when Bobby finally gets himself together to join the main plot, the story flows so good. It just keeps going and going, one thing happening right after the other. The best part is Pendragon <i>finally</i> got himself together, and I finally start seeing why he's the Lead Traveler. Yes. YES. He's finally somewhat adept, and his flow with Alder (Denduron Traveler) is great. Heck, Alder is great. I love Alder. And Patrick (Third Earth Traveler) also gets pumped up, and does his part as a Traveler.<br /><br />And the ending, hobey, the ending. Let's just say I'm glad I'm reading this after the book series is completed, because I'm gonna dive right into the next one.<br /><br />And so we go.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2228866403420690170" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
